Take thrash metal, hardcore, death metal, classic heavy metal and a tinge of progressive rock/metal mixed in with even a smaller one of alternative rock/country and throw it into a cauldron. Allow it to melt, creating a bubbling molten lava of steel. Take Trivium's all 3 past records and throw them into the cauldron. Stir vigorously. Take Metallica's, Megadeth's, Machine Head's and Iron Maiden's best elements and add to the mixture. Hint: you will NOT need any Killswitch Engage this time around. Allow it to simmer and sit until cold and solid. Salt and pepper to taste. Serve best cold.<br /><br />What separates this record from the Trivium's past is the incredible variety in tracks themselves. Granted, you can still hear the same band in all 11 songs (no instrumentals this time), but you are given something else to munch on in every one. Moreover, the album FEELS like an epic, conceptual piece. Some people have complained that it starts off like one of Metallica's classic records- with an acoustic segment, but this is done for the purpose of continuity with the last track on the album. The intro to \\"Kirisute  Gomen\\" is the main melody from the title track \\"Shogun\\". If there's any comparison, I would say Machine Head's \\"The Blackening\\" uses the same motive and it is no coincidence, because that album had a huge influence on \\"Shogun\\". From the first minute, then, you are treated to a variety of sounds and influences, Matt Heafy switching seamlessly between his clean vocals of Crusade, clean vocals of Ascendancy, his \\"screams\\" of Ascendancy and a new style, a brutal death metal growl that would not be out of place on a Malevolent Creation record. Just listen to the mid-break in insurrection- pure sulphur! This is another interesting thing about the new Trivium- every song has radio friendly and even rock parts to it, but they are encased in a heavy - as - Godzilla's - balls mixture of death/thrash core wall of sound. The riffs and melodies on this album are simply top notch, the band exceeding themselves creatively and in performance. Every member of Trivium gave it all on this one and it shows. The catchy parts are so hummable, they will torture you with earworms for all eternity, and the solos rival the best of 80's thrash/death metal. Matt Heafy has evolved from a mediocre sound-like everybody else-in metalcore vocalist to one of the best and most versatile in metal. His clean vocal performance is top notch and his growls are brutal as brutality itself. What Matt does vocally on this album just has to be heard to be believed.  Finally, Matt has written the best lyrics of any Trivium record.<br /><br />Since all the songs get 5/5 from me, individual rating would have been redundant. Onto the songs, a brief description of the best elements in each:<br />1. \\"Kirisute Gomen\\".<br />This is both Crusade and Ascendancy sounding song. The best moments are mid-song melodic chorus/break and the harmonies of the bridge, and of course, lyrics (\\"...I'll take their f@#$ing head!\\") Another new element is the brutal, low tuned guitar sound, which reminds me of Hypocrisy.<br />2. \\"Torn Between Scylla and Charybdis\\"<br />My personal favorite track of the album, it has amazing guitarwork, if slightly on the progressive side, two choruses, one mid-paced and one slow, amazing bass solo worthy of Cliff Burton in the mid-part and this song is the most varied and complex, except for the title track.<br />3. \\"Down from the Sky\\"<br />This is the video-single, a good video, in my opinion. As for the song, it is one of the outstanding tracks on the record, it features the opening country/metal? riff, that ultra-brutal death metal growl from Matt, great bridge before the chorus which is also very addictive. Great musicianship, overall.<br />4. \\"Into the Mouth of Hell We March\\"<br />I told my friend Chris, if you don't like this song, youdon't like metal, man. This just a pure melodic thrashfest reminiscent of Rust in Peace/Countdown to Extinction Megadeth and \\"Somewhere in Time\\" Iron Maiden. My second favorite.<br />5. \\"Throes of Perdition\\"<br />This one will no doubt polarize many with its super-radio friendly chorus which sounds like...Nickelback. Even Matt sounds like Chad Croeger on this one, on purpose, I think. But that is not all that is to it. The song also features ultra-brutal guitar breakdowns and riffs with that Hypocrisy sound. So even if you want to put this on the radio, the teenagers will still freak out over the \\"scary man growling over the sounds of the construction site\\" or something like that. I like this song, it's different, it's still Trivium and it shows that they are capable of much more than thrash/metal core. And, of course, everything is superbly executed here and that friendly chorus WILL haunt you.<br />6. \\"Insurrection\\"<br />Thrash metal at its finest. This would not have been out of place on the Crusade, but it's way better than that record. There is a lot of \\"Embers to Inferno\\" on it, too. The mid part, as I have mentioned earlier, has that ultra-brutal Malevolent Creation death metal break. Brutal.<br />7. \\"The Calamity\\"<br />Another example of Crusade done better, mixed in with \\"Embers...\\" this reminds me of \\"Countdown to Extinction\\" Megadeth. It has an absolutely addictive, superb melody in the chorus. Matt soars vocally and gutarwise.<br />8. \\"He Who Spawned the Furies\\"<br />Another weird one. This has been influenced by Opeth and doom metal. Different than the rest, which to me, is a plus. I don't like to hear one song and then 10 worse versions of the same on the record (cough, new All That Remains, cough)<br />9. \\"Of Prometheus and the Crucifix\\"<br />This ties in with track 2 for my favorite track on the album. Spectacular, highly original, and the best chorus on the record with superb melody and guitars. Matt exceeds his own ability as vocalist, and I mean the clean vocals. He is one of the best in the biz, now. Awesome, simply, awesome.<br />10. \\"Like Calisto to a Star in Heaven\\"<br />More melodic bliss. It builds up on the last song but stands on its own. Uses some weird spoken vocals in the middle. Some thrash crescendos in between, reminiscent, again, of Trivium's first album.<br />11. \\"Shogun\\"<br />The crown jewel of \\"Shogun\\". 11 minutes of unbelievable musicianship and vocal prowess. It has all the best elements of Trivium, and serves as a summary to all we have heard on this album. It is Trivium's most ambitious, most creative song to date. Heavily influenced by \\"The Burning Red\\" Machine Head as well as MH last album. And then, Matt breaks into this Hetfield-sound-alike ballad-like vocal line that sounds like \\"Load\\"! It sounds so eerie, as though Hetfield actually guest singing on the record! But, like with imitation of Chad Croeger's earlier, I believe Matt has done it for fun, and I appreciate his sense of humor in this matter. And it fits songs perfectly. It ends like \\"Embers to Inferno\\" with a mournful, melodic riff, at a slightly faster pace. Ladies and gentlemen you have just heard the album of the year 2008.<br /><br />When I reviewed \\"The Crusade\\", I was very disappointed with it, but I expressed my hope (the same reserved for the next All that Remains record now) that Trivium will recover from that setback. I am happy to announce that they have not only met, but far exceeded my expectations for their new music. Personally, I thought they would never top excellent \\"Ascendancy\\". I was wrong. They have easily done that, while, in my opinion, totally burying the legend of Metallicas and Megadeths of the world (most certainly those of recent, at least). Why? Because they did not try to sound like them but better, they decided to stick to what makes them sound best-like Trivium.<br /><br />Now this is what happens when an incredibly talented band swallows their pride, recovers and learns from their good butnot great last recording (The Crusade), looks back to the best of their creative past (Ascendancy, Embers to Inferno), abandons their insane sound-alike contest with Metallica (without shaking off all the healthy influence), allows appropriate time between last record and a new one (over 2 years, unlike barely a year between  Ascendancy and the Crusade), incorporates all the best elements of their past records, combines their sound with experimentation not only from metal, and, in the end, creates their masterpiece. It is a work complete, not one note too much or too little, a quintessence of a band's over 5 years in music business/art. Shogun is a record that even Trivium themselves will have a hard time topping. This is how modern metal should evolve, drawing from other genres while still staying, essentially, metal. Otherwise, it becomes stale and a parody of itself. I am aware that we have yet to hear the new Unearth, God Forbid and Omnium Gatherum records, but for me, \\"Shogun\\" is easily a contender for the album of the year as of now. And Matt Heafy IS the Chuck Shuldiner (Death) of the 21 century, period.0. \\"Like Calisto to a Star in Heaven\\"   More melodic bliss. It builds up on the last song but stands on its own. Uses some weird spoken vocals in the middle. Some thrash crescendos in between, reminiscent, again, of Trivium's first album.   11. \\"Shogun\\"  The crown jewel of \\"Shogun\\". 11 minutes of unbelievable musicianship and vocal prowess. It has all the best elements of Trivium, and serves as a summary to all we have heard on this album. It is Trivium's most ambitious, most creative song to date. Heavily influenced by \\"The Burning Red\\" Machine Head as well as MH last album. And then, Matt breaks into this Hetfield-sound-alike ballad-like vocal line that sounds like \\"Load\\"! It sounds so eerie, as though Hetfield actually guest singing on the record! But, like with imitation of Chad Croeger's earlier, I believe Matt has done it for fun, and I appreciate his sense of humor in this matter. And it fits songs perfectly. It ends like \\"Embers to Inferno\\" with a mournful, melodic riff, at a slightly faster pace. Ladies and gentlemen you have just heard the album of the year 2008.    When I reviewed \\"The Crusade\\", I was very disappointed with it, but I expressed my hope (the same reserved for the next All that Remains record now) that Trivium will recover from that setback. I am happy to announce that they have not only met, but far exceeded my expectations for their new music. Personally, I thought they would never top excellent \\"Ascendancy\\". I was wrong. They have easily done that, while, in my opinion, totally burying the legend of Metallicas and Megadeths of the world (most certainly those of recent, at least). Why? Because they did not try to sound like them but better, they decided to stick to what makes them sound best-like Trivium.      Now this is what happens when an incredibly talented band swallows their pride, recovers and learns from their good but not great last recording (The Crusade), looks back to the best of their creative past (Ascendancy, Embers to Inferno), abandons their insane sound-alike contest with Metallica (without shaking off all the healthy influence), allows appropriate time between last record and a new one (over 2 years, unlike barely a year between  Ascendancy and the Crusade), incorporates all the best elements of their past records, combines their sound with experimentation not only from metal, and, in the end, creates their masterpiece. It is a work complete, not one note too much or too little, a quintessence of a band's over 5 years in music business/art. Shogun is a record that even Trivium themselves will have a hard time topping. This is how modern metal should evolve, drawing from other genres while still staying, essentially, metal. Otherwise, it becomes stale and a parody of itself. I am aware that we have yet to hear the new Unearth, God Forbid and Omnium Gatherum records, but for me, \\"Shogun\\" is easily a contender for the album of the year as of now. And Matt Heafy IS the Chuck Shuldiner (Death) of the 21 century, period.
B0017R5UAA|5.0|Fleet Foxes' debut full length album is a pleasant, folksy good time. It doesn't really reach the heights that some more intense bands do, but the combination of good acoustic guitar work, alternately catchy and haunting vocal harmonies, and unique song structures make for a record really worth listening too.  The hippie-looking Robin Pecknold is probably the band's driving force, writing all the lyrics and taking charge with the vocals, but you get the feeling they just like playing together as a group and working together to create one memorable sound.  I had heard that this album was one of the year's best indie releases, and decided to check the video for \\"White Winter Hymnal\\" on Youtube.  I was a bit surprised by what I was hearing, because it doesn't sound like something from this year at all, but still captivated by it, and I shortly found out that this same thought carried throughout each of the tracks.    From the near prog-like constant shift in pace of \\"Sun it Rises\\" to the solitary howling at the end of \\"Oliver James\\", every song does something unique while still fitting the band's central feeling.  I almost feel like I've heard some of these before, and I'm sure that's partly because it's hard to come up with unique music these days, but that quality of familiarity is part of its appeal to me.  It's hard to really describe what makes each song good, because it's never a single hook or element, it's always the sum of the parts.  Some favorites are \\"Ragged Wood\\", \\"Quite Houses\\", \\"Your Protector\\", and \\"Blue Ridge Mountains\\".  It's really one of those albums that has to be listened to as one experience and not a bunch of disparate tracks to throw on your iPod's shuffle.  Although \\"White Winter Hymnal\\" is still pretty awesome by itself.

Unfortunately, Microsoft's mild tweaks to the Xbox controller were brilliant, and Sony's few additions were useless except for the wireless capability, and it even took them a while to get around to bringing back the rumble feature.<br /><br />Microsoft smartly resisted overhauling their controller and recognized how to perfect the basic design by downsizing, rounding off some hard edges, and moving the black and white buttons as well-sized, nimbly responsive shoulder buttons. The PS3 controller is still a fine controller, and the best one for the Playstation, but Microsoft stepped out of character and actually made a brilliantly improved product (along with the Xbox itself) that now has, to my mind, taken the throne as best designed controller.<br /><br />This controller coupled with a nice rubbery silicon covering for it makes it the perfect controller for the PS3, just avoid the Six-axis use whenver you can -- more gimmick than benefit.

1847245455|3.0|I think the problem with this novel, which other reviewers have ably summarised, is that it is an artificial construct.<br /><br />I mean, I didn't find the story boring, tne number of characters excessive or the plot (there are in fact two; which is the main one in human terms, possible future reader?) difficult to follow, as other negative revs have. On the contrary, for me the narration flowed agreeably, the twists were unexpected, and the book didn't pretend to be what it was not (a semibrow literary piece). But it, or rather its main characters, are implausible: cardboard, not flesh-and bone. At all times you're aware you're reading a story, not something that could have been real life. Here we revert to an Ellery Queen type of novel without its intellectual tease, which leaves ... nothing.<br />So the book is basically a kid's one (although full of episodes a real kid souldn't read), with heroes that are decent, loyal, intelligent, charming, truthful -one of them agonizes over a moral dilemma that could find a place in Lincoln's hagiography-, with liberal worldviews, etc.; with a convenient deus ex machina that finds out everything that's needed at the drop of a hat; with corrupt -and worse- financial tycoons/villains; with real dark, dark imperturbable villains with awful perversions and insatiable bloodlusts; and with a closing tirade about the evils of finance (for maximum impact the book should have been published after the current Wall Street turmoil) with words lifted almost straight out of Keynes.<br /><br />Perhaps I could summarise it all with three words: it's a politically correct book. Nothing against them, of course, and for that (and the research it inconspicuously packs) I give it three stars. But if you have read Lehane's \\"Gone, baby, gone\\" (a book less grisly by far, but that poses a real moral dilemma), you'll understand what I mean.
